  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bb1014f7-e746-4284-886e-4edaeddaa260'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer6797027615311692730">Nita Callahan is at the end of her rope because of the bullies who've been hounding her at school... until she discovers a mysterious library book that promises her the chance to become a wizard. But she has no idea of the difference that taking the Wizard's Oath is going to make in her life. Shortly, in company with fellow beginner-wizard Kit Rodriguez, Nita's catapulted </span>
  <span id="freeText6797027615311692730" style="display:none">Nita Callahan is at the end of her rope because of the bullies who've been hounding her at school... until she discovers a mysterious library book that promises her the chance to become a wizard. But she has no idea of the difference that taking the Wizard's Oath is going to make in her life. Shortly, in company with fellow beginner-wizard Kit Rodriguez, Nita's catapulted into what will be the adventure of a lifetime—if she and Kit can both live through it. For every wizard's career starts with an Ordeal in which he or she must challenge the one power in the universe that hates wizardry more than anything else: the Lone Power that invented death and turned it loose in the worlds. Plunged into a dark and deadly alternate New York full of the Lone One's creatures, Kit and Nita must venture into the very heart of darkness to find the stolen, legendary Book of Night with Moon. Only with the dangerous power of the wizardly Book do they have a chance to save not just their own lives, but their world...</span>
  <a data-text-id="6797027615311692730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2018444449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2018444449" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2018444449?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385293051" href="/book/show/1062961.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=inbetweenworld">inbetweenworld</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=secret-histories">secret-histories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2018444449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15685420699479191575">So you want to stop being bullied, you just want some time to yourself, to read, to do what you want to do, to even make a friend maybe? You find a book and it tells you how. Your book will take you places. Dealing with bullies after reading this book becomes such a small thing. Being the person you want to be and doing the things you want to do is so much more important!<br/><br/>So you want to learn how to do wizardly things, talk to trees and suchlike, make things happen, meet new beings, maybe find th</span>
  <span id="freeText15685420699479191575" style="display:none">So you want to stop being bullied, you just want some time to yourself, to read, to do what you want to do, to even make a friend maybe? You find a book and it tells you how. Your book will take you places. Dealing with bullies after reading this book becomes such a small thing. Being the person you want to be and doing the things you want to do is so much more important!<br /><br />So you want to learn how to do wizardly things, talk to trees and suchlike, make things happen, meet new beings, maybe find that lost pen? Your book will show you how. It will turn magic into science and you will summon not a demon but a star; your new friend will have his own familiar too, not a beast but a car. A star and a car. They will take you far!<br /><br />So you want to discover new worlds? How about Hell? Or a twisted version of our world full of horror and hopelessness which may as well be hell. It may not be the adventure you wanted but it is an adventure nonetheless. You and your friend will have to figure things out, and very quickly - it's a good thing you both are smart. You will learn important lessons on this adventure, like sometimes people you love will die. And that's a hard lesson to learn!<br /><br />So you saw this on kindle unlimited for the remarkable price of free and you thought, hey that's on my list, why not? You also thought that this would be pretty okay, you haven't heard much about it but then there's this surprisingly real slice of life and this surprising bit of diversity (in the 80s!) and then that other bit of diversity (a gay couple? maybe? in an 80s book for kids!) and the surprisingly science-y way of using magic and the surprisingly bleak and hallucinogenic adventure that comes from searching for a lost pen (of all things!) and the surprising lack of adults or aslans to the rescue (but lots of trees and statues!) and then, surprise surprise, you've realized you just started a whole new series that promises a whole lot of pleasure!<br /><br />So you want to read a kid's book that starts off like any good kid's book but slowly becomes something more resonant than you expected, darker and more tragic and yet still light and life-affirming? I suggest you read this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15685420699479191575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2182424070" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2182424070" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2182424070?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780152162504" href="/book/show/1062958.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of A Wrinkle in Time</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to carol.  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/6894205-allie">Allie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=multi-culti">multi-culti</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy-ya">urban-fantasy-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2182424070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14232171922664629853">Why yes, yes I do.<br/><br/>Based on the title, I expected something rather light and possibly silly. What I got was something more substantial, an old middle-grade book/YA book that suddenly had me recalling <i>A Wrinkle in Time</i> and <i>A Swiftly Tilting Planet.</i> Somehow I missed this one when I was younger, which is too bad. An enthusiastic review from a friend (thanks, Allie!) alerted me to this deficiency and I decided to rectify it.<br/><b><br/>"She strolled between shelves, looking at titles, smiling as she met old frie</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14232171922664629853" style="display:none">Why yes, yes I do.<br /><br />Based on the title, I expected something rather light and possibly silly. What I got was something more substantial, an old middle-grade book/YA book that suddenly had me recalling <i>A Wrinkle in Time</i> and <i>A Swiftly Tilting Planet.</i> Somehow I missed this one when I was younger, which is too bad. An enthusiastic review from a friend (thanks, Allie!) alerted me to this deficiency and I decided to rectify it.<br /><b><br />"She strolled between shelves, looking at titles, smiling as she met old friends--books she had read three times or five times or a dozen. Just a title, or an author's name, would be enough to summon up happy images. Strange creatures like phoenixes and psammeads, moving under smoking London daylight of a hundred years before... starships and new worlds and the limitless vistas of interstellar night..."<br /></b><br />Nita, short for Juanita, is regularly bullied and abused by neighborhood kids, finding herself almost helpless to prevent it. As she is running away, she darts into the library for safety and finds herself walking through the children's section, greeting books like old friends. One jumps out at her: So You Want to Be a Wizard? and she finds herself intrigued by what she reads. Perhaps it can help keep her safe from bullying? The wizard's book is divided into sections, and the read book follows those guidelines. 'Prologue,' 'Preliminary Exercises,' Research and Development,' etc. In short order, she meets another bullied kid, Kat, and starts working with him to retrieve a pen stolen from Nita in her latest attack. Events quickly escalate.<br /><br />There's a lot to like here; a male and female lead that aren't involved in a romantic relationship, Kat's Latino heritage, parents that are supportive but mildly inept, astrophysics, mild fart humor, and kids saving the world. I thought the meta-themes of responsibility, compassion and choices well done. Added bonus for talking to trees and a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[dragon with mild dementia <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I loved the affection for libraries and books so evident in the first chapter. I thought the dialogue had an organic feel.<br /><br />What isn't to like is that Duane seems to still have some period sexism going on, generally possibly explained by the fact that Kat discovers his book sooner, except that it still felt... off. There's also a lot of extraneous writing where a paragraph literally takes up a page and a half, particularly at the end battle. Plot development is a bit disjointed; I think even as a youth, it would have seemed odd to me to draw my sand in the line over an astronaut pen, but maybe not. The skill level of the two young wizards grows exponentially; they literally prepare for the big adventure by reading thirty chapters in one night. Because a lot of times Nita and Kat use Wizard Speech, the dialogue markers are in parenthesis, which may be confusing to less sophisticated readers.<br /><br />On the balance, however, good completely outweighs the bad. I bet I would have loved it when I was younger, and I can absolutely see giving the sequel a try.<br /><br />Three and a half stars, rounding up at the request of Young carol.<br /><br />See also mark monday's review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2018444449?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14232171922664629853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16257233497429969861" style="display:none">This is sort of an American, dark and urban version of Harry Potter. While browsing shelves at the library, Nita discovers a book with the title "So You Want to Be a Wizard" She takes it as a joke, but it turns out to be the real deal. The spells work and she actually is learning to be a wizard.<br /><br />It turns out that this is the way wizards are trained. Their textbooks seek out those with the talent. Nita soon finds another wizard named Kit and they go on a really twisted and somewhat scary adventure to a very dark and creepy world.<br /><br />While on the surface, you might think it sounds a lot like Harry Potter, but it isn't. The book has a totally different tone and many people who like HP books don't like this one. I liked it though. It's a totally different "world" with totally different magic and it feels more like a comic book than anything else.</span>

<div id="review_29292264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29292264" />
    <a title="Daniella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1397575-daniella"><img alt="Daniella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576642933p2/1397575.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29292264?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniella" href="/user/show/1397575-daniella">Daniella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780152162504" href="/book/show/1062958.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1397575-daniella?shelf=rereadable">rereadable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1397575-daniella?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1397575-daniella?shelf=contemporary-fantasy">contemporary-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1397575-daniella?shelf=book-challenge-2009">book-challenge-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1397575-daniella?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1397575-daniella?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1397575-daniella?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1397575-daniella?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29292264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18274978938544259878"><i>"Dear Artificer, I’ve blown my quanta and gone to the Good Place!"</i><br/><br/>I'm so glad that I decided to re-read <i>So You Want to Be a Wizard</i> as part of my self-imposed book challenge for this year. I'd almost forgotten how much I love this book!<br/><br/>In fact, I love it so much that I almost <i>couldn't</i> read it again. At first, I would read a couple of pages and have to put the book down because I'd get all teary and junk. Not because it's sad (although it does have its moments), but because I would remember how mu</span>
  <span id="freeText18274978938544259878" style="display:none"><i>"Dear Artificer, I’ve blown my quanta and gone to the Good Place!"</i><br /><br />I'm so glad that I decided to re-read <i>So You Want to Be a Wizard</i> as part of my self-imposed book challenge for this year. I'd almost forgotten how much I love this book!<br /><br />In fact, I love it so much that I almost <i>couldn't</i> read it again. At first, I would read a couple of pages and have to put the book down because I'd get all teary and junk. Not because it's sad (although it does have its moments), but because I would remember how much the story touched me the first time I read it. And it still does.<br /><br />There are so many things in this book that, even as an adult, I can relate to: from Nita's isolation and finding solace in books to the desire to become, to be and to <i>do</i> something more, something beyond imagining, being so strong that even danger and death seem worth the risk. I cannot even begin to count how many times, or how intensely, I've wished throughout my life for something to come along and turn my world upside down, set me off on some crazy ass adventure and make everything new and exciting. And reading about an introverted, socially awkward, oft-misunderstood geek who stumbles across a mysterious book and suddenly finds herself immersed in a world (or two) of wizardry and wonder (and some terror and heartache) allows me to live my fantasy vicariously through a younger, fictional, sort-of alter ego.<br /><br />Another thing I absolutely adore about this book--and the Young Wizards series in general--is that Diane Duane never assumes that the readers (her target audience being kids roughly, I'd say, 10-14) won't "get it" just because they're young. She doesn't dumb anything down, doesn't shy away from using or making up big words, and she doesn't water down her prose into that succinct but ineloquent simplicity sometimes found in young adult novels. Yet she's managed to weave a tale that is not only beautiful and sometimes lyrical in its elegance (I truly loved how she described the trees talking in <i>leafrustle</i> and <i>fireflicker</i>), but also accessible.<br /><br />Duane also deserves kudos for creating one of <i>the</i> most original characters ever. I mean, in what other book are you going to find a freaking <i>white hole</i> as a central character? And, oh, how I adore Fred.<br /><br /><i>"You people are so fragile. A little gamma radiation will ruin your whole day, it seems."</i><br /><br />Who can <i>not</i> love a wise-cracking and often endearingly clueless space phenomenon who has a bad habit of spontaneously emitting cosmic rays? Not I, my friends, not I.<br /><br />Did I mention that I adore this book? I do. And if you're looking for a fast-paced, action-packed, strangely reaffirming adventure to sink your teeth into, or if you're trying to find something to fill the gaping wound...er...void left after <i>Harry Potter and the Book That Tore My Heart to Pieces, Covered Them in Petrol, Set Them on Fire and Danced a Merry Jig All Over the Bloody Ashes, Goddamn You, Joann</i> (otherwise known as <i>Deathly Hallows</i>), I highly recommend SYWBW and the rest of the Young Wizards series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18274978938544259878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2914275867" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2914275867" />
    <a title="Ash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57274851-ash"><img alt="Ash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603895397p2/57274851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2914275867?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash" href="/user/show/57274851-ash">Ash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780152049409" href="/book/show/176519.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">nerds</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57274851-ash?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57274851-ash?shelf=lgbt-side-character">lgbt-side-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57274851-ash?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57274851-ash?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2914275867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17433885727526148705">Diane Duane’s <i>Young Wizards</i> series is an old favorite. I’m pretty sure this is my third time rereading it, and I enjoy it just as much - if not more - each time.<br/><br/><i>So You Want to Be a Wizard</i> defies age categorization. The protagonist, Nita, is thirteen, and from the outside, everything about the book seems to fit neatly into the middle grade category. But once you start reading, you run into some language and concepts that, when I first read this book as a preteen, went over my head. I would compar</span>
  <span id="freeText17433885727526148705" style="display:none">Diane Duane’s <i>Young Wizards</i> series is an old favorite. I’m pretty sure this is my third time rereading it, and I enjoy it just as much - if not more - each time.<br /><br /><i>So You Want to Be a Wizard</i> defies age categorization. The protagonist, Nita, is thirteen, and from the outside, everything about the book seems to fit neatly into the middle grade category. But once you start reading, you run into some language and concepts that, when I first read this book as a preteen, went over my head. I would compare it to Madeleine L’Engle’s books in that respect. The end result is a series I’ve been able to enjoy at every stage of life.<br /><br />In <i>So You Want to Be a Wizard</i>, Duane introduces a complex magic system and a multifaceted world that unfolds gradually with each book. She blends fantasy and science fiction in a way that’s destined to appeal to fans of both genres, like myself. My younger self was drawn in by the relatable characters and with every subsequent reread I’ve developed a stronger grasp of subject matter that previously escaped me. There’s nothing quite like a book you can revisit again and again and still gain something from each time.<br /><br />Speaking of relatable characters, I have to gush about the protagonist, Nita Callahan. Nita is a bookish young teen, bullied by her peers for her smart mouth and nerdy inclinations. I had a lot in common with Nita the first time I read this book and I think that’s why she’s still, to this day, one of my favorite characters. Her fellow young wizard, Kit Rodriguez, is equally likable, and each side character comes to life with a unique personality.<br /><br />The only flaw in this book – and it’s not even enough of a flaw for me to take a star off my rating – is that Duane has a tendency to wax philosophical, and it can get a bit much. In small doses, it adds to the grandiosity of the story, but when laid on too thick, it’s distracting and overwrought. There are only a few places in <i>So You Want to Be a Wizard</i> where this happens, though, so I’m able to overlook it.<br /><br />I would describe this book as charming and eccentric, yet simultaneously dark and deep. I’ve never read anything else like it. I’m looking forward to rereading book two. This series is definitely a comfort series for me, one I reread again and again because it brings me so much joy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17433885727526148705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11723572440898609518">The magic and wizardry content in this book was just too strange. It's totally possible to write about things that are different from what we experience in this world, but to write them in a way that you understand what's going on. In this book, though she uses analogies that don't help make things any clearer. When I stopped reading, for example, the 2 young wizards are creating a thing to plug a hole in a thing to keep out a grey cloud that they somehow know wants to eat them (clearly I couldn</span>
  <span id="freeText11723572440898609518" style="display:none">The magic and wizardry content in this book was just too strange. It's totally possible to write about things that are different from what we experience in this world, but to write them in a way that you understand what's going on. In this book, though she uses analogies that don't help make things any clearer. When I stopped reading, for example, the 2 young wizards are creating a thing to plug a hole in a thing to keep out a grey cloud that they somehow know wants to eat them (clearly I couldn't tell what was going on). The analogy she used to explain what the situation was like, paraphrased: "It was like a cement rose unfolding, or like being at a party where everyone wants to tell you their life story." I just was stumped by how those analogies work together, and also by how that was supposed to explain the situation.</span>

  <span id="freeText15932577069669150935" style="display:none">When the young readers in my acquaintance complain that there aren't more Harry Potter books to read, I like to suggest this series.<br />I usually start the campaign with a few questions to get them interested.<br />"What if kid wizards couldn't tell their families about their powers?"<br />"What if they had to risk their lives in secret to keep the world safe?"<br /><br /><br />I find the pre-teen and teen characters in this series to be much more engaging and realistic than the self-centered, clueless and common sense-lacking characters found in much juvenile fiction.<br /><br />I also fell that the way Ms. Duane portrays courage, friendship, trust and sacrifice in these books teaches a positive lesson to the young readers in an entertaining (and almost subliminal) way.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5737038606005464242">Reading this book, I wished I could time travel. I would hand this book to my younger self, when I was Nita's age. Because much as I liked this book as an adult, I know that if I'd first read this in middle school, I would have loved it.<br/><br/>It is a good book, a very good book. I take nothing away from Duane, because I think she hit every mark nearly perfectly. And I did enjoy reading it, even if I'm not hooked.   <span id="freeText5737038606005464242" style="display:none">Reading this book, I wished I could time travel. I would hand this book to my younger self, when I was Nita's age. Because much as I liked this book as an adult, I know that if I'd first read this in middle school, I would have loved it.<br /><br />It is a good book, a very good book. I take nothing away from Duane, because I think she hit every mark nearly perfectly. And I did enjoy reading it, even if I'm not hooked. Her system of magic is interesting, basically talking the world into doing what you want it to do. It sounds simple and intuitive, but deep enough to take years, or a lifetime, to truly master. And yet, I know that everything I liked about this book I would have loved if I'd read it at age twelve, and much that I was apathetic towards I would have liked. Some books should just hit you at the right time of your life, or miss their chance to really take hold.</span>

<div id="review_78536535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78536535" />
    <a title="Adam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2923960-adam"><img alt="Adam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573094203p2/2923960.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78536535?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam" href="/user/show/2923960-adam">Adam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People from the 1950's, Trash Fantasy lovers, young kids with nothing else to read,</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Adam by: </span>
      Mrs. (Sandra?) Laviolette, Alex Katigbak
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2923960-adam?shelf=fantasy-and-science-fiction">fantasy-and-science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78536535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18034304646342771253">I started reading this book for the first time when I was grade 8 and I couldn't really get into it. I've finally figured out why.<br/><br/>I'm reading it again because it was in my house and I needed something to read, and the dialogue feels forced and VERY dated. It's almost a condescending mockery of how kids talk. The ideas in it are really interesting, but they're described by thirteen year-olds who talk like little kids, instead of adults, so the magic is being sucked out of... well... the magic. <br/><br/>An</span>
  <span id="freeText18034304646342771253" style="display:none">I started reading this book for the first time when I was grade 8 and I couldn't really get into it. I've finally figured out why.<br /><br />I'm reading it again because it was in my house and I needed something to read, and the dialogue feels forced and VERY dated. It's almost a condescending mockery of how kids talk. The ideas in it are really interesting, but they're described by thirteen year-olds who talk like little kids, instead of adults, so the magic is being sucked out of... well... the magic. <br /><br />And then just to completely throw the reader, the other characters all talk like incredibly wise people, and 'Fred's' language seems pretty advanced. There are passages where Nita describes Entropy, which (at least at my school) wasn't tackled until the 11th grade, but she's supposed to be 13...<br /><br />My initial impression is that the novel can't decide what age demographic it wants to aim at, and it's all over the place.<br /><br /><br />Oh and Carl and Tom don't seem like just room mates. Just sayin'. <br /><br />***********************************************<br /><br />Nov 22nd 2009<br /><br />This book hits a huge wall around page 200 and becomes slow.<br />Like, really, really, really, slow.<br />It's like a snail and a jar of marmalade reproduced and then that offspring mated with a sloth/really-boring-Sunday-school-lecture hybrid.<br />I'm not even sure how Duane pulled that off because there is so much action in the second half that it could have filled up three novels worth of climaxes.<br /><br />There were a couple of moments where I had to go back and reread passages, because the characters suddenly had an intense knowledge of magic for no reason (Well... the reason was that they read about 30 chapters virtually overnight and somehow memorized it all). It really took me out of the experience.<br /><br />Also, younger wizards are stronger than older wizards? uhh... that's one of the dumbest concepts I've ever heard of.<br />Here's why:<br /><br />1. That would mean that as time progresses the wizard would get weaker, which is not only ridiculous, but makes no sense. The more you practice something, the better you get. How could you possibly be good at something you've never done before, and then not improve through practice? How frustrating would that be?!<br /><br />2. It's a cheap plot device. <i>"Why are Nita and Kit able to do all this stuff, but the other wizards can't?" "'cause they're younger, thasswhy!"</i><br /><br />3. It means that as the book series progresses (...yuck...), the stories would, theoretically, get more boring because the magic is less complex.<br /><br /><br />The majority of the second half of the book feels like Nita whining for Kit to save her, and he does. The world they fall into is supposed to be filled with nightmarish creatures and scare Nita and Kit (and presumably anyone who accidentally winds up there), but I've felt more chills walking in downtown Montréal at night. Perytons, which were supposed to be horrifying creatures of blah blah blah, were bland and anything but menacing.<br /><br />Nita is virtually useless, except to calm down Fred, who's almost as useless, though occasionally he'll fart and scare the bad guys. At least Fred's good for a laugh!<br /><br />Nita freaks out one moment, then immediately pulls herself together enough to comfort Fred... umm.. what?<br /><br />Fred is the ONLY redeeming character in this book, and even that statement is a stretch.<br /><br />If you really want to experience magic, check out Harry Potter or the Bartimaeus trilogy.<br /><br />And saying "This book is older than Harry Potter!" is a BS argument because a lack of Potter influence doesn't excuse <i>SYWTBAW</i> from being this crappy. It could have set precedent so we'd compare Harry Potter to <i>SYWTBAW</i>. Instead it's the other way around.<br /><br />Seriously Nita, Kit, you did all that to get a pen back?!<br /><br /><br /><br />PS: Redeeming features:<br /><br />-Rant-ability<br />-Different Magic system (though poorly described)<br />-Fred<br />-LOL unintended but ever present Misogynism, perfect if you have to do a project on "sexist themes in Children's literature" or something of the like.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18034304646342771253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1619324081" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1619324081" />
    <a title="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out"><img alt="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473475487p2/16915869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1619324081?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~" href="/user/show/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out">Linda ~ they got the mustard out! ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9780613360777" href="/book/show/1062965.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=multiracial-cultural">multiracial-cultural</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=grade-school">grade-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=borrowed-then-bought">borrowed-then-bought</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=bullies">bullies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16915869-linda-they-got-the-mustard-out?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1619324081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12232823523923302746">GODDAMMIT DIANE DUANE STOP PUNCHING ME IN THE HEART!<br/><br/>It's a children's book, they said. <br/>It's like Harry Potter but in America, they said.<br/>You'll have a good time, they said.<br/><br/>THEY ALL LIED! I'M NOT CRYING YOU'RE CRYING!<br/><br/>There was a time when this book was about a girl, Nita, getting bullied at school and having her pen stolen - and this was the happy fun times. This book becomes so much more when she hides in a library and finds a book about wizardry. A book that materialized there just for her to di</span>
  <span id="freeText12232823523923302746" style="display:none">GODDAMMIT DIANE DUANE STOP PUNCHING ME IN THE HEART!<br /><br />It's a children's book, they said. <br />It's like Harry Potter but in America, they said.<br />You'll have a good time, they said.<br /><br />THEY ALL LIED! I'M NOT CRYING YOU'RE CRYING!<br /><br />There was a time when this book was about a girl, Nita, getting bullied at school and having her pen stolen - and this was the happy fun times. This book becomes so much more when she hides in a library and finds a book about wizardry. A book that materialized there just for her to discover. She soon finds another young wizard, Kit, who is also being bullied because of his accent and his brown skin. They befriend each other and start learning magic together, and then horrible and wonderful things start to happen.<br /><br />First, this is NOT Harry Potter. I don't know if JK Rowlings read this series before writing her own, but there are some elements that are similar in both. Aside from the obvious (magic) there is a one-who-must-not-be-named, dragons, time travel, and two protagonists who just don't fit in and they're in school together. But that's where the similarities end. The magic here is rooted in the principles of science, the wizards are charged with slowing the destruction of the universe (all of them), and Nita and Kit have to deal with all this while going to school, dealing with bullies and hiding this from their families. Oh, and there's a white hole named Fred, and that's the least absurd thing that happens in this book. There are Advisories, older wizards who are past their "freelancing" years and now advise younger wizards while going about ordinary lives. Potential wizards can choose for themselves if they want to take on the mantle of wizard - and they can put it aside again if they no longer feel up to the task. <br /><br />Duane borrows from fantasy, horror, science fiction and mythology to create her world. There are a couple of hiccups along the way, but for the most part the world-building is amazing here, and the prose is breathtaking. Nita and Kit (and Fred) are fully developed characters and get to go on their own personal journeys. They're friends and equals, despite being a year apart (Nita's older), different genders and different races. None of that stuff matters to them. What matters is that they have each other's backs, they encourage each other, and they both have strengths they can utilize as they fight the Destroyer - who eats stars out of spite. I was fully immersed as the action started to pick up, and then I didn't want to put it down, even when Duane punched a whole in my chest, tore out my heart and proceeded to squeeze it before my eyes.<br /><br />This is such a cool and amazing world Duane has created here in just one book. I don't know how I missed this series growing up, but I'm glad I'm reading it now. There is a lot of nuance here I'm sure I would've missed as a kid, and it would be hard to fully appreciate this world without picking up on that stuff. Also, the nightmare fuel. So much nightmare fuel. God, what are the other nine going to bring? I am not ready.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12232823523923302746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90575053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90575053" />
    <a title="Lolly&#39;s Library" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2649865-lolly-s-library"><img alt="Lolly&#39;s Library" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503734420p2/2649865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90575053?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lolly&#39;s Library" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lolly&#39;s Library" href="/user/show/2649865-lolly-s-library">Lolly&#39;s Library</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780152162504" href="/book/show/1062958.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649865-lolly-s-library?shelf=juvenile-fantasy">juvenile-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649865-lolly-s-library?shelf=borrowed-from-library">borrowed-from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649865-lolly-s-library?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90575053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7169715540293909733">I must've been too busy reading Diana Wynne Jones and Madeleine L'Engle, because I'd never heard of this series growing up. It was only in the past couple of years that it came to my attention. I have to say, I'm not all that impressed. Part of the problem is the fact that the book feels dated. Usually when that happens, the story is able to carry me along so that I don't notice things like Dictaphones and typewriters (non-self-correcting ones, at that). Not with this book. I blame most of that </span>
  <span id="freeText7169715540293909733" style="display:none">I must've been too busy reading Diana Wynne Jones and Madeleine L'Engle, because I'd never heard of this series growing up. It was only in the past couple of years that it came to my attention. I have to say, I'm not all that impressed. Part of the problem is the fact that the book feels dated. Usually when that happens, the story is able to carry me along so that I don't notice things like Dictaphones and typewriters (non-self-correcting ones, at that). Not with this book. I blame most of that on the "magic" used in the story; it seemed more like physics or calculus to me. I'm sorry, but when I want to read about physics, I'll read Stephen Hawking. I don't want to stumble through it in a childrens' book. It's not the fact that magic is equated with science that gave me pause, it's the manner in which the author narrated its use. The analogies and descriptions she gave of its workings had me scratching my head, rereading paragraph after paragraph, and always with the same result: "Huh? What the hell is she talking about?" The only way I got through it was to gloss over such descriptions: "Okay, they did something and now they're in a parallel world... Oh, look, cars that act like animals!" I'll also repeat what several have said before concerning the sexist attitude represented in the story; Nita seemed to require an awful lot of aid from her fellow (male, of course) wizard, Kit. She spent most of her time deferring to him, aiding his spells, looking to him for answers. Puh-lease. Not to mention the dumb-ass concept of younger wizards having more power (what?). What a lame plot device to explain the two kids' prowess with their wizardly powers.<br /><br />There are a few other nitpicky points of dislike which I won't go into detail here. The only bit that really was intriguing and quite original was the character of Fred, the white hole thingy (yes, that's a techinical term). His was the most well-rounded and charismatic character in the book, with the Lotus not far behind in terms of likeability. It's pretty sad when one feels a stronger connection to non-human characters than to the human ones about which the story (supposedly) revolves.<br /><br />I will be fair and give the next book a go. Perhaps the series gets better as the characters develop. If I'm wrong, however, I'll happily forgo the rest of the series and return to the books of Diana Wynne Jones and Madeleine L'Engle, forgetting I ever heard of Diane Duane. 2.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7169715540293909733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_216301994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/216301994" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/216301994?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=children-s-and-ya">children-s-and-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer216301994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3134864740888773098">I’ve been told to try these so often that I more or less assumed the recommendation would be apt, and got a bundle of the whole series in one of Diane Duane’s website sales. Unfortunately, something about this doesn’t work for me — I guess it feels too random and immature? Stuff like ‘Fred’, the ‘white hole’, who is the opposite of a black hole, and some of the logic of how magic worked just… I didn’t feel hooked by it. Once I got to the white hole burping up whole cars, I was more or less done;</span>
  <span id="freeText3134864740888773098" style="display:none">I’ve been told to try these so often that I more or less assumed the recommendation would be apt, and got a bundle of the whole series in one of Diane Duane’s website sales. Unfortunately, something about this doesn’t work for me — I guess it feels too random and immature? Stuff like ‘Fred’, the ‘white hole’, who is the opposite of a black hole, and some of the logic of how magic worked just… I didn’t feel hooked by it. Once I got to the white hole burping up whole cars, I was more or less done; I just skimmed the rest.<br /><br />I do actually like parts of the set-up: the idea of the book that starts the main character’s journey is pretty neat, for example, and I didn’t read the characters as just default white kids from the start — even if Kit Rodriguez’s name wasn’t a probable giveaway. I think maybe if I’d first read it when I was younger, and had that flexibility of imagination, I wouldn’t have questioned it so much and could have enjoyed it now if I was rereading it. Unfortunately, I come to this as a 27 year old about to get married, and so I just can’t engage with it on that level.<br /><br />Not something I would recommend to someone my own age, but I might very well pass it to a kid young enough to feel the magic of waiting for your Hogwarts letter, or scanning the library shelves for books about what you can be when you grow up and finding a mysterious book which at first might seem like a joke, but turns out all too real…<br /><br /><a href="http://breathesbooks.com/2016/06/26/review-so-you-want-to-be-a-wizard/" rel="nofollow noopener">Originally posted here.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3134864740888773098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3288081902" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3288081902" />
    <a title="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods"><img alt="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602607922p2/29163734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3288081902?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" href="/user/show/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods">Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780152012397" href="/book/show/1062960.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods?shelf=books-featuring-libraries">books-featuring-libraries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3288081902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4059558937786712549">Is "middle grade urban fantasy" a thing? <br/><br/>I read this in a collection of the first three novels in this series, titled <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242794.Support_Your_Local_Wizard__Young_Wizards___1_3_' title='Support Your Local Wizard (Young Wizards, #1-3) by Diane Duane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Support Your Local Wizard</a> and you have <i>gots</i> to see this cover art (embiggen as needed):<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242794.Support_Your_Local_Wizard__Young_Wizards___1_3_' title='Support Your Local Wizard (Young Wizards, #1-3) by Diane Duane' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1343558463l/242794._SX50_.jpg' alt='Support Your Local Wizard (Young Wizards, #1-3) by Diane Duane' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This thing is exemplary of the aesthetic that <i>Stranger Things</i> draws from. I mean, that's basically Barb (RIP) lying on the floor. And those pleated pants! You may be able to see the troll pencil-topper on the right. To me the biggest issue is why they are wearing their running shoes inside </span>
  <span id="freeText4059558937786712549" style="display:none">Is "middle grade urban fantasy" a thing? <br><br>I read this in a collection of the first three novels in this series, titled <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242794.Support_Your_Local_Wizard__Young_Wizards___1_3_" title="Support Your Local Wizard (Young Wizards, #1-3) by Diane Duane" rel="nofollow noopener">Support Your Local Wizard</a> and you have <i>gots</i> to see this cover art (embiggen as needed):<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/242794.Support_Your_Local_Wizard__Young_Wizards___1_3_" title="Support Your Local Wizard (Young Wizards, #1-3) by Diane Duane" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1343558463l/242794._SX50_.jpg" alt="Support Your Local Wizard (Young Wizards, #1-3) by Diane Duane" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This thing is exemplary of the aesthetic that <i>Stranger Things</i> draws from. I mean, that's basically Barb (RIP) lying on the floor. And those pleated pants! You may be able to see the troll pencil-topper on the right. To me the biggest issue is why they are wearing their running shoes inside the bedroom. <br><br>The period aesthetic is all over the text too. Lotus Esprit, anyone? If you're still not clear on what period this book is from, just consider the dedication from the sequel:<blockquote>Heartfelt thanks go to Neil Harris and his erstwhile comrades at Commodore, who went crazy hooking up a desperate writer's computer to one of their printers, and who helped her hit her deadline.</blockquote>The kicker for me is this bizarrely liberal concept of bullying. Thirteen-year-old Nita (short for Juanita) is routinely beat up by the more popular girls, leaving her with black eyes, swollen knee joints from targeted stomping, and more. Her parents are, like, shrug, "whatchoo gonna do?". To me this is far beyond bullying, this is felony assault, and today I would hope that the parents are calling the police and suing the crap out of the assaulter's parents. Be Best, people. <br><br>To avoid another such beating, Nita ducks into her favorite place, <i>the library</i> (yay!) where she comes across a book telling the reader how to be a wizard. She eventually decides it's not a joke, and after her first attempt to utilize her new knowledge, meets also-thirteen-year-old Kit (short for Christopher, everything was short for something in the 80's I guess) who is just a little bit ahead of her in his training, and in just one week they are ready to master cosmos- and reality-spanning forces in an effort to retrieve Nita's space pen. Okay, it's about more than that. <br><br>It's a tough book to pin down for age appropriateness these days. It's middle grade-ish in appeal but teen-ish in comprehension. I imagine it would have resonated most strongly in its day with kids like the protagonists; kind, brainier than was socially acceptable at the time, and honest enough not to hide it. These are kids who know offhand how long it takes sunlight to reach the Earth. The book has lots of dated cosmology, some real terms and some invented for the book. The author's affection for her characters is evident. Nita and Kit are a good pairing. The story continues through several sequels which I will not be reading. It's a sweet and smart and caring book, but it is so specific to its era of publication that it could never be a classic. <br><br>Kudos to whomever put this book facing out in an open space on my public library's SF/F shelf (catalogued in the adult section somehow), because that cover art is pure 80's gold.<br><br><b>UPDATE 4/24/2020: </b>I was surprised to find a copy of this book on my home shelf! I was straightening up the children's paperbacks shelf and there it was! It either came from a library book sale or from neighbors. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4059558937786712549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2385094706" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2385094706" />
    <a title="Ariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22465719-ariel"><img alt="Ariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508179437p2/22465719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2385094706?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariel" href="/user/show/22465719-ariel">Ariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/39691447-so-you-want-to-be-a-wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22465719-ariel?shelf=elementary-middle-school">elementary-middle-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2385094706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15950603407396095923"><i>”But you’re wizards, you should know how terrible a power belief is, especially in the wrong hands—and how do you tell which hands are wrong? Believe something and the Universe is on its way to being changed. Because you’ve changed, by believing. Once you’ve changed, other things start to follow. Isn’t that the way it works?”</i><br/><br/><i> “..for darkness only made the light seem brighter.”</i><br/><br/><i> “We do what we have to, to live. Sometimes that means breaking a rock’s heart, or pushing roots down into a ground that </i></span>
  <span id="freeText15950603407396095923" style="display:none"><i>”But you’re wizards, you should know how terrible a power belief is, especially in the wrong hands—and how do you tell which hands are wrong? Believe something and the Universe is on its way to being changed. Because you’ve changed, by believing. Once you’ve changed, other things start to follow. Isn’t that the way it works?”</i><br /><br /><i> “..for darkness only made the light seem brighter.”</i><br /><br /><i> “We do what we have to, to live. Sometimes that means breaking a rock’s heart, or pushing roots down into a ground that screams against the intrusion. But we never forget what we’re doing. As for you—how else should our children climb to the stars but up our branches? We made our peace with that fact a long time ago, that we would be used and maybe forgotten. So be it. What you learn in your climbing will make all the life on this planet greater, more precious.”</i><br /><br />Isn’t it amazing that these lines of wisdom were spat out by a tree and a white hole?<br /><br />Gosh, that does not make this series sound flattering at all, but let me tell you a thing, about how this is one of the greatest middle-grade series that has ever existed. Everyone needs to read it, and I mean everyone. This was my series growing up. A lot of people can say Harry Potter, or Hunger Games, or what have you. But Young Wizards? This was/is my JAM.<br /><br />I must have read the first five books, over and over, a dozen times at least, just patiently waiting for each new book in the series to arrive and to add to my collection like the demented dragon I am. What a series. What a series that speaks of heavy topics: life and death, sacrifice and the meaning of sacrifice in a physical and emotional sense; of children growing beyond their years and forced to grow too fast and to learn too quickly what heartache and sorrow mean; what good and evil is and is there ever really a distinction or just hundreds of shades of gray? And what questions do you ask the Transcendent Pig if you ever come across him?<br /><br />When I first read <b>So You Want to be a Wizard</b>, I can’t tell you how many times I searched for my own copy of the Index at the library, hoping my own fingers would get caught in the binding of a special book that only I knew was more than it seemed beneath the covers. Alas, that hasn’t happened (YET), but I still dream on that one day it will.<br /><br />What I really appreciate about the New Millennium Editions vs the original published copies is the story is still the same, just with additional details and a “better/makes more sense” of a timeline. If you read the original editions (still as good as ever), there’s a bit of dissonance in terms of timelines. Duane published a majority of these in the 90s and early 2000s and so the later books are different in terms of technology and such that it feels ‘weird’ if you read them in a continual lineup. I highly recommend find the NME on Diane Duane’s personal website where they are DRM free!<br /><br />Re-reading <b>So You Want to be a Wizard</b> was like coming home after a long, long time away. I had forgotten how special these books were to me and the last time that I had read the series from beginning to end. This is also the first time I find myself taking a crack at the NME (New Millennium Editions) and finding that the additional bits of detail or changes add to the story and give it more of a cohesive flow and understanding. (Just imagine JKR updating Harry Potter with a modern day timeline and you’ll know what I mean.)<br /><br />Highly, highly recommend this wonderful, amazing, beautiful series for all.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15950603407396095923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2174903975" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2174903975" />
    <a title="Allie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6894205-allie"><img alt="Allie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538540055p2/6894205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2174903975?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allie" href="/user/show/6894205-allie">Allie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6894205-allie?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6894205-allie?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2174903975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1634153217892189324">Long before Harry Potter, there was Diane Duane’s Young Wizards series, about two lonely tweens who become wizards and best friends in a quest to save the world(s). I devoured these books in middle school, although I didn’t fully understand all of the scientific concepts that the author weaves into the story...including entropy, black holes, string theory, and the lifespan of stars. I just remember being fascinated by the exciting adventures of Kit and Nita. Re-reading this book as an adult, I’m</span>
  <span id="freeText1634153217892189324" style="display:none">Long before Harry Potter, there was Diane Duane’s Young Wizards series, about two lonely tweens who become wizards and best friends in a quest to save the world(s). I devoured these books in middle school, although I didn’t fully understand all of the scientific concepts that the author weaves into the story...including entropy, black holes, string theory, and the lifespan of stars. I just remember being fascinated by the exciting adventures of Kit and Nita. Re-reading this book as an adult, I’m even more impressed by how intelligent and interesting the story is for readers of all ages. <br /><br />When the book starts, Nina is hiding from school bullies in the children’s section of the library. Tucked into the “career” books about becoming a doctor or firefighter, she discovers a guide to becoming a wizard. But like the knights of old, she has to first take an oath and complete an “Ordeal” that proves her valor. The work of wizards is to fight entropy throughout the universe, which is embodied in the figure of the Lone One. Drawing on myths of Lucifer, the Lone One is a fallen version of a bright star who turned his back on the Powers That Be and introduced death into the world. After taking her oath, Nita and another young wizard, a boy named Kit, face the Lone One in a corrupted alternate version of Manhattan. Accompanied by a friendly star (which has left most of its mass elsewhere) they face predatory helicopters, man-eating cars, and a very old dragon with memory loss in their quest to return a special book to its rightful place. <br /><br />The world building is thoughtful, the characters are engaging, and almost every chapter has some neat and creative idea about the practice of wizardry. (I loved the world gates for travel between universes, which are managed by sentient cats in New York’s Grand Central Station.) Other books have since “borrowed” some of Duane’s ideas, such as the Speech, the universal language of power that wizards use to persuade animals, objects, and even space to do the wishes of the speaker. But I think my favorite part of the story is the celebration of friendship across stereotypical boundaries. <br /><br />Highly recommended for readers of all ages and for families to read together.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1634153217892189324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_373136889" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/373136889" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/373136889?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780152162504" href="/book/show/1062958.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christina (A Reader of Fictions) by: </span>
      Alexa Wang
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=series-not-finishing">series-not-finishing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer373136889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer854058387557051692">Conveniently, the very first book chosen for me in my new regular posting series, Sadie Hawkins' Sunday, just happened to be a book I already had in my personal collection. This series first came onto my radar when I was looking for readalikes for Harry Potter. I did enjoy this one (thanks Alexa!) and I'm glad I got a chance to dig into my massive collection of unread books.<br/><br/>The first thing that you should probably know is that this book was first published in 1983, long before Harry Potter. The </span>
  <span id="freeText854058387557051692" style="display:none">Conveniently, the very first book chosen for me in my new regular posting series, Sadie Hawkins' Sunday, just happened to be a book I already had in my personal collection. This series first came onto my radar when I was looking for readalikes for Harry Potter. I did enjoy this one (thanks Alexa!) and I'm glad I got a chance to dig into my massive collection of unread books.<br /><br />The first thing that you should probably know is that this book was first published in 1983, long before Harry Potter. The book definitely does have quite a few similarities, and, those looking for Potter readalikes, might love this, but Duane was not one of the authors trying to ride Rowlings' success. I wonder if Rowling had read these, since certain things, like the villain being referred to as You-Know-Who were incredibly similar.<br /><br />For all of that, though, So You Want to Be a Wizard reminds me much more heavily of Madeleine L'Engle's A Wrinkle in Time. There is a lot of complicated vocabulary and scientific terminology within the pages of this book that would probably be targeted to a middle grade audience today. I mean, do you know what a 'temporospatial claudication' is? I sure don't. The science-y weirdness and good versus evil messages conveyed in this novel had me thinking constantly of L'Engle's classic work. In fact, I think that if you love A Wrinkle in Time, you really ought to check this series out. I loved A Wrinkle in Time when I was younger, but was not charmed by it particularly when I reread it. Science just really is not my thing, so I cannot appreciate a lot of what happens in either. <br /><br />My favorite aspects of the book center around the power of the written word and love of books. There are a bunch of amazing quotes to that effect (check my favorite quote for one example). Plus, the whole concept is great. Every library has tons of those "So You Want to Be..." books, and I love how Duane built fantasy knowledge into such a seemingly simple thing.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this clever device also serves as a method for info-dumping the ways of wizardry on the reader. Nita takes the library book home and devours it, attention rapt, but I did not find her reading the book nearly so enticing. This goes on for chapters. Duane tries to draw the reader in by including Nita's reactions to her reading, but these sections still dragged for me. I also feel like both Nita and Kit pick up their magical knowledge too quickly and easily. They read through their books once and can do a number of powerful spells after just a bit of practice. Plus, the spells are supposed to leave them tired, but they spend literally the last half of the book running around and doing spell after spell, even though one wiped them out the afternoon before.<br /><br />As a reader, I just really struggle with books that don't place a focus on characterization. I would have loved to know more about Nita and Kit, and their daily lives. They're both clearly smart kids, and have both suffered from bullying. Rather than watching them go on a mission to retrieve Nita's stolen pen, which is really the quest of the book though it does snowball, I would have liked to see them have more personal growth, rather than just magical.<br /><br />I'm really glad to have read this, because I can see how influential it has been on young adult literature, and I admire Duane for her creativity and her diverse characters. However, I do not plan to continue with the series, since I do not think I'm the ideal audience for these books. If you love A Wrinkle in Time, though, seriously, I think you will love this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="854058387557051692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
