<div id="review_164357114" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164357114" />
    <a title="Amy Eye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4597412-amy-eye"><img alt="Amy Eye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344625409p2/4597412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164357114?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Eye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Eye" href="/user/show/4597412-amy-eye">Amy Eye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780152049409" href="/book/show/176519.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164357114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12944280830412568614">Everyone one has seen the books like "So you wanna be a (fill in the blank)". Nita gets lucky enough to find one that is to help her along her way to become a wizard! This is the dream of half the children in America. Nita decides she wants to use this book to help her fend off the bullies who constantly beat her up and leave her nursing her wounds and her pride on a daily basis. <br/><br/>One day as she is learning about her new found magical abilities, she runs into Kit, also a new wizard. They put thei</span>
  <span id="freeText12944280830412568614" style="display:none">Everyone one has seen the books like "So you wanna be a (fill in the blank)". Nita gets lucky enough to find one that is to help her along her way to become a wizard! This is the dream of half the children in America. Nita decides she wants to use this book to help her fend off the bullies who constantly beat her up and leave her nursing her wounds and her pride on a daily basis. <br /><br />One day as she is learning about her new found magical abilities, she runs into Kit, also a new wizard. They put their heads together and in their first meeting perform a spell together that will benefit them both, or so they had hoped. In this first excursion, they pick up Fred, an adorable new friend who was once a black hole. While picking up Fred, they discover a hideous world they are anxious to escape from, the feelings of terror and vileness are palpable. <br /><br />Back in their own reality, they children embark on a journey that not only leads them to powers they never dreamed of, it leads them straight back to the horrible reality they so recently escaped. The children struggle to free themselves from a land where fire hydrants eat pigeons, and helicopters try to eat humans. <br /><br />I was enthralled with the book at the onset. The synopsis of the book had me ready for a marvelous fantastic adventure. What this turned out to be was more of sci-fi book with the terms magic thrown around in it in order to get in on the latest wizard bandwagon. I have heard before of magic having a place in the scientific realm - the whole shebang. But when they are transported to a land where everything is mechanical, and everything with a gear in it is evil, I feel like I am in a PG rated Terminator movie. I appreciate the original idea of it, but it simply wasn't to my taste. Someone had suggested this to me after I mentioned I wanted something to help me get over my Harry Potter fixation. If you are looking for a fantastic world of that nature, this is not the book for you. If you are looking for a fantastic world that will lead you more on the Battle Star Galactica course this is what you are looking for.<br /><br />When I look for magic, I'm not ready or wanting to read about mechanical things, it throws off my groove. I'm not saying this was a poorly written book, it is written very well, and anyone who is interested in more "technical" magic will fall in love with this book. But for my entertainment buck, I'll pass on the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12944280830412568614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_180983003" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180983003" />
    <a title="Nathaniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5713428-nathaniel"><img alt="Nathaniel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180983003?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathaniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathaniel" href="/user/show/5713428-nathaniel">Nathaniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780152162504" href="/book/show/1062958.So_You_Want_to_Be_a_Wizard">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180983003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12937743307821828780">I remember reading this book for the first time and finding an entire new world opened up to me. I was ten then, in search, as the main character here was, for something deeper; something fantastic in everyday life. I read this book, the second, and the third in the series in such quick succession that I couldn't believe I'd actually managed to make my brain process the words that fast, and I was hooked forever on fantasy. <br/><br/>Years later I came back to this book and opened it up, and the magic was </span>
  <span id="freeText12937743307821828780" style="display:none">I remember reading this book for the first time and finding an entire new world opened up to me. I was ten then, in search, as the main character here was, for something deeper; something fantastic in everyday life. I read this book, the second, and the third in the series in such quick succession that I couldn't believe I'd actually managed to make my brain process the words that fast, and I was hooked forever on fantasy. <br /><br />Years later I came back to this book and opened it up, and the magic was still there. I'm a writer now, more than in part due to this book, and I've realized just what an amazing author Duane is. I've read a few other reviews on here that complain that the book feels dated, that the characters have dialogue that doesn't feel real, that the descriptions don't describe, and I can only wonder at what they are talking about. To me the characters are as vivid as any in adult fiction. More so, in fact. They have dreams, fears, longings, and their dialogue is laced with little flavors of slang that I can still imagine being used somewhere today. <br /><br />And as for the descriptions, the entirety of the final chapters still makes me shiver. There's one in particular that I love, one that evokes the old ancient infinity of the universe:<br /><br />"She was turning the pages without even thinking about it, finding the place that spoke of creation and rebellion and war among the stars---the words that had once before broken the terrible destroying storm of death and darkness that the angry Starstuffer had raised to break the new-made worlds and freeze the seas where life was growing, an eternity ago."<br /><br />It's a book I love dearly and continue to cherish every time I pick it up. Highly, highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12937743307821828780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62300618?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Destinee Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Destinee Sutton" href="/user/show/90661-destinee-sutton">Destinee Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90661-destinee-sutton?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90661-destinee-sutton?shelf=harry-potter-alternative">harry-potter-alternative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90661-destinee-sutton?shelf=tween">tween</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62300618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6879224029893166794">Part of what makes great fantasy is a great setting, i.e. an original other world that feels real even though it's so different from the world we inhabit. I found this book totally lacking in that department. Nita and Kit (whose names and personalities are too similar--I kept getting them mixed up as I read) start in the real world as normal kids. They meet when they realize they're both aspiring wizards and then they go looking for Nita's lost pen and end up in this horrible, dark alternate uni</span>
  <span id="freeText6879224029893166794" style="display:none">Part of what makes great fantasy is a great setting, i.e. an original other world that feels real even though it's so different from the world we inhabit. I found this book totally lacking in that department. Nita and Kit (whose names and personalities are too similar--I kept getting them mixed up as I read) start in the real world as normal kids. They meet when they realize they're both aspiring wizards and then they go looking for Nita's lost pen and end up in this horrible, dark alternate universe where they are chased by monstrous living helicopters and cars. <br /><br />Here's my biggest problem: The story got so deep so fast. The kids have only been wizards for a few weeks and suddenly they're totally alone and fighting for their lives to find the most important book in the universe? I'm barely getting to know the world Duane has created and we're already at what feels like the climax! It's like someone asking to marry you on the second date. And this date is not making you laugh. In fact, he's a little hard to follow and seems to be speaking a different language that he doesn't bother explaining to you. You are getting bored and tuning him out for whole paragraphs, but there's something about him that reminds you of an old boyfriend you still think of fondly (maybe his name was Harry? Or Charles Wallace?) and so you cut him some slack. <br /><br />But let's face it: he is not what you want. It's time to move on. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6879224029893166794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_419320324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer4449132693858996618">I think this is the worst book I ever read. Only reason I finished it is because it was so short (and even then it took me a while to slog through it). Very surprised there was enough interest to create a series after this terrible first book. Some highlights:<br/> <br/>p. 10: "A wizard's business is to conserve energy </span>
  <span id="freeText4449132693858996618" style="display:none">I think this is the worst book I ever read. Only reason I finished it is because it was so short (and even then it took me a while to slog through it). Didn't even realize it was part of a series when I was reading it, as I had forgotten the reason I had checked it out was because the 6th book in the series made the ALA Teen Top Ten List. Very surprised there was enough interest to create a series after this terrible first book. Some highlights:<br /> <br />p. 10: "A wizard's business is to conserve energy - to keep it from being wasted. On the simplest level this includes such unmagical-looking actions as paying one's bills on time, turning off the lights when you go out, and supporting the people around you in getting their lives to work."<br /><br />Oh my gosh, I wish I had given up on the book right there after that heavy-handed ridiculousness. On page 45 they magically bring a talking white hole to Earth that they name Fred. Yeah, this story keeps getting better and better. In addition, even though they have this white hole they brought to Earth, and they learn that the book that keeps everything in existence is missing, all the main character can think about is getting her ordinary pen back. Some more quotes:<br /><br />p. 47: Fred talking: "It stopped bobbing, stared at her as if she had said something derogatory. (Do I look like a hole?)<br />p. 74:Fred talking: (...Not since I was a black hole, certainly. Black holes swallow everything, but a white hole's business is emission.)<br /><br />Wait a second, he thought being referred to as a white hole was a derogatory term, but then uses it to reference himself just a few pages later!? Yeah, this book was not good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4449132693858996618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608720125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11254583774711807178">I wanted to like this. I really did. The beginning was super promising, a totally unique form of magic and how the wizard came across it. I was here for Nita, totally dug the fact that it was a male/female best friendship and they were both PoC. I was here for pretty much everything about this book.<br/><br/>Except for the fact that it is so...incredibly...boring. I quit at about 60% in when my brain was just screaming "ENOOUGH! ENOUGH ALREADY!" every time I thought about picking it up. Scenes were draggi</span>
  <span id="freeText11254583774711807178" style="display:none">I wanted to like this. I really did. The beginning was super promising, a totally unique form of magic and how the wizard came across it. I was here for Nita, totally dug the fact that it was a male/female best friendship and they were both PoC. I was here for pretty much everything about this book.<br /><br />Except for the fact that it is so...incredibly...boring. I quit at about 60% in when my brain was just screaming "ENOOUGH! ENOUGH ALREADY!" every time I thought about picking it up. Scenes were dragging, there was no real plot line to speak of, and when it stopped being magical happy fun time with Kit and Nita I was like...meh. I'm out.<br /><br />Sorry! I gave it a shot but on to the next young wizard series.</span>

<div id="review_3436226808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3436226808" />
    <a title="John Loyd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3716161-john-loyd"><img alt="John Loyd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475255722p2/3716161.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3436226808?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Loyd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Loyd" href="/user/show/3716161-john-loyd">John Loyd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3436226808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10304846519442154294">Nita has been bullied, black eyes and more, by Joanne. She doesn't fight back, only tries to run away. During one of these escape attempts she hides in the library and finds a book she had never seen before--So You Want to be a Wizard--she starts looking through it. If only magic were real... It's a library, she borrows it. A day or two later says the Oath, and the finds her name in the book under novices. After another encounter with Joanne, she can't find her pen. She takes the book into the w</span>
  <span id="freeText10304846519442154294" style="display:none">Nita has been bullied, black eyes and more, by Joanne. She doesn't fight back, only tries to run away. During one of these escape attempts she hides in the library and finds a book she had never seen before--So You Want to be a Wizard--she starts looking through it. If only magic were real... It's a library, she borrows it. A day or two later says the Oath, and the finds her name in the book under novices. After another encounter with Joanne, she can't find her pen. She takes the book into the woods to read. The trees start talking to her, say there's another wizard around. She meets Kit, a twelve year old boy who got his book a couple weeks ago.<br /><br />Kit wants to do a spell that will keep him from being bullied, Nita wants to find her pen. They decide to combine efforts. They go to some strange and malevolent dimension. To get back they need to balance the spell. They end up bring back a point of light with them. A sentient star (or white hole) who left it's mass somewhere else. They call it Fred. The three go to see advisors the next day. The advisors fix a problem, but say they have to go to the worldgate to get Nita's pen back.<br /><br />This is the first of three books in this omnibus edition and there are more than ten in the series. Here they are novices and they go up against The Lone Power. I'm interested to see where they go from there. The timeline seemed to be, Nita found the book on a Saturday, took the Oath in the next day or two, met Kit (and Fred) the next day or so. They had to wait until the next Saturday to go to the worldgate and ended that night. It's a lot to take in very quickly. How does Nita go from no knowledge of magic to being a practitioner in a week. Also not much chance to decide the wizards are the good guys. The way the Oath is stated pretty much decides that, but I'm thinking are their good vs. bad wizards? It's YA and a few details are geared toward that market. Fred being a talking white hole. Kids can accept it better, less disbelief. Being that this is world like our own, I'd like it to be more sci-fi and less fantasy. All these mentions of landmarks in New York City is really neat for people who know that geography, OK for the rest of us, but it emphasizes more that it's a world like ours. 4 of 5 stars and I'll definitely read the next two in this omnibus. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10304846519442154294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cLdrdSoYH2O/hgyVqumwlccwNz+lTBQyrG7vxGEM8E8wRc0hqlKoNrvDMSn7ivdTJEMmRhnlneBtvAIWGgLfOQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9YWwEHwk/cK1fWFwMoKmHDlk8jo+GvJ101j1+fMgWNW1dxZE/G5Kl7E4XMxj4eHa2hfjQ4Kze6cSihgriC53ow==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer840885350185219118">Diane Duane has been a writer of science fiction, fantasy, TV and film for more than forty years.<br/><br/>Besides the 1980's creation of the Young Wizards fantasy series for which she's best known, the "Middle Kingdoms" epic fantasy series, and numerous stand-alone fantasy or science fiction novels, her career has included extensive work in the Star Trek TM universe, and many scripts for live-action and an</span>
  <span id="freeText840885350185219118" style="display:none">Diane Duane has been a writer of science fiction, fantasy, TV and film for more than forty years.<br /><br />Besides the 1980's creation of the Young Wizards fantasy series for which she's best known, the "Middle Kingdoms" epic fantasy series, and numerous stand-alone fantasy or science fiction novels, her career has included extensive work in the Star Trek TM universe, and many scripts for live-action and animated TV series on both sides of the Atlantic, as well as work in comics and computer games. She has spent a fair amount of time on the New York Times Bestseller List, and has picked up various awards and award nominations here and there.<br /><br />She lives in County Wicklow, in Ireland, with her husband of more than thirty years, the screenwriter and novelist Peter Morwood.<br /> <br />Her favorite color is blue, her favorite food is a weird kind of Swiss scrambled-potato dish called maluns, she was born in a Year of the Dragon, and her sign is "Runway 24 Left, Hold For Clearance."<br /><br />(From her official website)</span>
